# Analysis

## Ground Truth (GT)
The GT expression is:
$$f(t, P) = 0.877 \cdot P \cdot \sin(0.5672 \cdot t) + 0.7014 \cdot (1 - P/65.75) \cdot P$$

Expanding:
$$f(t, P) = 0.877 \cdot P \cdot \sin(0.5672 \cdot t) + 0.7014 \cdot P - 0.01067 \cdot P^2$$

So the GT has the form:
$$f(t, P) = a \cdot P \cdot \sin(b \cdot t) + c \cdot P + d \cdot P^2$$

where $a, b, c, d$ are specific constants. The basis functions are: $P \cdot \sin(bt)$, $P$, and $P^2$.

## Candidate 1:
$$P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 \sin(c_3 t + c_4)$$

This has basis functions: $P^2$, $P$, $P \sin(c_3 t + c_4)$.

Setting $c_4 = 0$, this becomes $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 \sin(c_3 t)$, which matches the GT form exactly.

Set $c_0 = -0.01067$, $c_1 = 0.7014$, $c_2 = 0.877$, $c_3 = 0.5672$, $c_4 = 0$.

**This is a MATCH.**

- GT: $0.877 P \sin(0.5672t) + 0.7014P - 0.01067P^2$
- Candidate 1 with chosen constants: $-0.01067P^2 + 0.7014P + 0.877P\sin(0.5672t + 0)$

## Candidate 2:
$$P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 \sin(c_3 + c_4 t) + c_5 t + c_6 \sin(c_4 t + c_7)$$

Setting $c_5 = 0$ and $c_6 = 0$ eliminates the extra terms $c_5 t$ and $c_6 \sin(c_4 t + c_7)$. Then we get:
$$P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 \sin(c_3 + c_4 t)$$

Setting $c_3 = 0$, this matches the GT. **This is also a MATCH.**

Many of the other candidates involve $\log(P \cdot c + 1)$ terms. For these to match the GT, the coefficients of all log terms must be zero. Let me check a few:

## Candidates 3-50 (with log or other extra terms):
Most candidates from 3 onward have terms like $\log(P \cdot c + 1)$ or rational expressions $1/(P + c_1)$. 

For candidates with $\log$ terms: setting $c_6 = 0$ (or equivalent) makes $\log(0 \cdot P + 1) = \log(1) = 0$, eliminating all log terms. Then we need to check if the remaining structure can match.

For candidates with $/(P + c_1)$ denominators: multiplying through, we'd need the structure to reduce to $P^2 + P + P\sin(...)$. Many of these can work by setting $c_1 = 0$ (making the denominator just $P$), but then we'd need to check for division by zero issues and whether the remaining terms work.

For example, **Candidate 3** with $c_1 = 0$: all terms have $/(P + 0) = /P$, giving $P c_0 + P c_2 \sin(...) + c_5 \sin(...) + c_7 + c_8 \sin(...)/P + 1/P$. The $1/P$ and $\sin/P$ terms can't be zeroed without also zeroing wanted terms. So this requires more careful analysis, but since we already found matches, this is sufficient.
